    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

  <span id="freeText5612740994399983587" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter bizi diğer romancıların gitmeye cesaret edemediği, derin ve karanlık yerlere götürüyor. Günümüzün en cesur polisiye yazarlarından biri.”<br /><br /> - Tess Gerritsen<br /><br />“Amerika’nın en iyi polisiye yazarlarından biri.”<br /><br /> - The Washington Post<br /><br />Atlanta’nın varlıklı bir semtinde, güzel bir evde genç bir kız hunharca katledilmiş ve başka bir kız da kaçırılmıştır. Genç kızın annesi, cesedin başında bulduğu yabancıyı kendi elleriyle öldürür, ancak öldürdüğü kişi gerçekten kızının katili midir? Ya da öldürülen, kendi kızı mıdır?<br /><br />Olayı inceleyen iki dedektif Will Trent ve Faith Mitchell’ın zamana karşı yarışı başlar. Hem cinayeti aydınlatmak hem de kaçırılan genç kıza, henüz hayattayken ulaşmak zorundadırlar. Paramparça’da Karin Slaughter, iz peşinde geçen üç günün soluk kesen hikâyesini anlatıyor.<br /><br />Genç kuşağın en sevilen polisiye yazarlarından olan Karin Slaughter’ın kitapları dünya çapında 32 dile çevrildi, 30 milyon okura ulaştı. Paramparça, İngiltere ve Hollanda’da çok satanlar listesine bir numaradan girdi ve haftalarca kaldı.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/179863-i-have-read-all-the-karin-slaughter-books">I have read all the Karin Slaughter books, she&#39;s a very muscular writer who doesn&#39;t shy away from graphic descriptions always done in the service of the story. Love her tortured,fragile,fractured FBI agent Will Trent, he&#39;s a very compelling character and beautifully drawn. He continues to grow from one story to the next. No question here more of a statement.</a>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7305336242381460358">Start a book, call it Fractured<br/>Murder, mayhem, someone's captured <br/>Pressure builds, Trashcan battered <br/>2 of series, questions answered<br/>Writing, plot, clearly mastered <br/>Valued reading, Karin Slaughtered</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3415150712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7193476318113037224"><i>"Everyone had a reason for everything they did, even if that reason was sometimes stupidity."</i><br/><br/><b>A young girl is found brutally murdered. A mother who kills the alleged murderer. A missing girl. A scandalous and gruesome mess. It’s going to take one special individual to solve this crime: enter Will Trent.<br/><br/>Fractured, is a dark and gruesome mystery/thriller featuring Will Trent and Faith Martin. </b><br/><br/>The second installment of the series introduces Will Trent’s new partner, Faith Martin. Faith is a smart an</span>
  <span id="freeText7193476318113037224" style="display:none"><i>"Everyone had a reason for everything they did, even if that reason was sometimes stupidity."</i><br /><br /><b>A young girl is found brutally murdered. A mother who kills the alleged murderer. A missing girl. A scandalous and gruesome mess. It’s going to take one special individual to solve this crime: enter Will Trent.<br /><br />Fractured, is a dark and gruesome mystery/thriller featuring Will Trent and Faith Martin. </b><br /><br />The second installment of the series introduces Will Trent’s new partner, Faith Martin. Faith is a smart and dynamic character. I loved how she and Will played off each other, and I am looking forward to seeing how their working relationship and tentative friendship progress. <br /><br />Will has a personal connection to the case in more ways than one, making him especially vulnerable. I enjoyed seeing this side of him.<br /> <br />Overall, Fractured is another great addition to the series. The case is dark and embodies many different levels of disgustingness. <b> I am always fascinated by the little clues that Slaughter weaves in that fall right over my head, and this book was no exception. </b> It’s not as good as book one, Triptych, but still very good. Angie's character makes only a few appearances, which was fine by me! <b>The moments featuring Betty the dog made me smile. </b><br /><br />Onto book 3!</span>

<div id="review_1399348542" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399348542" />
    <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon"><img alt="♥Sharon♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417537732p2/12125670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399348542?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Sharon♥" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon">♥Sharon♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399348542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1193592808450677609"><br/><br/>I really need to write my reviews before starting my next book. I get distracted and I forget to come back. At the moment I am distracted with book #3 in this series and I love it so far!!<br/><br/>Fractured was another fantastic read. I found the plot to be just as engaging as I did in book #1 and the characters continue to intrigue me. Karin Slaughter writes her characters in such a way that she gives you slivers of their personalities, bits and pieces of their pasts and how each character connects to t</span>
  <span id="freeText1193592808450677609" style="display:none"><br><br>I really need to write my reviews before starting my next book. I get distracted and I forget to come back. At the moment I am distracted with book #3 in this series and I love it so far!!<br><br>Fractured was another fantastic read. I found the plot to be just as engaging as I did in book #1 and the characters continue to intrigue me. Karin Slaughter writes her characters in such a way that she gives you slivers of their personalities, bits and pieces of their pasts and how each character connects to the other and then she twists each of them in a way you might not expect. For me it just keeps my imagination ticking. I love it!<br><br>One of the characters that I am finding myself enjoying is Will’s boss <b>Amanda Wagner</b>, deputy director of the Georgia Bureau of Investigation’s. She is disliked but respected. She is that type of woman who could chew you up and spit you out. She is hard and rather rigid. I felt anxious when she was around Will. She always tested him, his strengths and his weaknesses. She had the ability to raise him up and the ability to tear him apart. But there was no mistaking that she was also his protector. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/amanda_zpsuyby7sff.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444788460i/16552607.jpg" alt=" photo amanda_zpsuyby7sff.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>We see a different side of <b>Special Agent Will Trent</b> in this one. With every layer that is peeled away my heart swells a little more. He really is an amazing and lovable man. He is awkward and a bit socially inept. There is something in him that drives his intensity and his craziness. He has this sixth sense with his surroundings and the people who cross his path and this continues to pique my curiosity as to who he really is. <br> <br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/will_zps7scmadek.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444788460i/16552608.jpg" alt=" photo will_zps7scmadek.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Added to this series is <b>Faith Mitchell</b> who is a cop that ends up being Will’s partner. I wonder what will develop between them. She is strong willed and not a person to just roll over or walk away from a challenge. She doesn’t coddle Will and that is a good thing. I look forward to what’s to come with her.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/faith_zpskhfqjqp6.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444788460i/16552609.jpg" alt=" photo faith_zpskhfqjqp6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I don’t want to say much about the plot for fear of giving something away. But in <b>Fractured</b> the plot centers on teenagers, strained families and pain no parent should be faced with. Teenagers are faced fitting in and finding their way. Life can be so confusing and one bad choice can be so destructive.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/teenager_zps4otwafbu.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444788460i/16552610._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo teenager_zps4otwafbu.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When the horror hits, everyone and everything comes in to question. Who do you believe and who do you trust? I had my YUCK moments and my EWW moments. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/trust-100273826-orig_zpsfqhw6kxv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444788460i/16552611.jpg" alt=" photo trust-100273826-orig_zpsfqhw6kxv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>A lot happens on Peachtree Street! Looking forward to more of this series and finding out every little bit about this guy Will Trent!!<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/large_atlanta2_zpswas9tsdv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444788460i/16552612.jpg" alt=" photo large_atlanta2_zpswas9tsdv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I was going to end my review without mentioning <b>Angie Polaski</b> but for better or worse she is someone whose is deeply connected to Will. I understand why she is part of his life but she doesn’t deserve to be, at least anymore. I don’t like her at all. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1193592808450677609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1160007196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1160007196" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1160007196?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=harper">harper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1160007196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9794972679291204094">Fractured by Karin Slaughter is a 2008 publication. <br/><br/><br/>This second book in the Will Trent series, is a complicated case involving the death of an unpopular girl, and the kidnapping of her affluent friend, Emma. <br/><br/>Will finds himself feeling a little off his game when it comes to light that he and Emma’s father have a shared history and Will must work on this case with a partner, Faith Williams, a woman who holds a grudge against him. <br/><br/>This crime story is complicated, sordid, and pretty lurid. The polic</span>
  <span id="freeText9794972679291204094" style="display:none">Fractured by Karin Slaughter is a 2008 publication. <br /><br /><br />This second book in the Will Trent series, is a complicated case involving the death of an unpopular girl, and the kidnapping of her affluent friend, Emma. <br /><br />Will finds himself feeling a little off his game when it comes to light that he and Emma’s father have a shared history and Will must work on this case with a partner, Faith Williams, a woman who holds a grudge against him. <br /><br />This crime story is complicated, sordid, and pretty lurid. The police procedural is interwoven into a complex family drama. Once more the devil is in the details, and Will eventually locks all the pieces together, to open a Pandora’s box of evil. <br /><br />This second installment was not quite as strong as the first, but it is still a very absorbing story, one that made me cringe on more than one occasion. I love how the story is cleverly woven together, piece by piece, connecting everything so seamlessly. <br /><br />I also like the attention the author gives to learning disorders and the difficulties those who live with these issues face. Will, of course, is a prime example, and his expertise in these matters actually comes in handy. <br /><br />I did kind of enjoy Will’s discomfiture at times, since he seems so smooth outwardly, at least, most of the time. He is certainly an enigma, and hard to figure out. I thought Faith really gave him a run for his money and kept him on his toes, which is good for him.<br /><br />Angie is not prominently featured in this installment and I am curious about the future of her relationship with Will. <br /><br />I found the family dramas added a layer of angst to the tense situation, as the inevitable blame game began, and marital discord became public knowledge. It is also a little bit of a character study, not so much on one particular person, but on a class of people, who have become accustomed to having their way, controlling situations, and making demands. Emma’s parents have no control over the investigation, but attempt to manipulate it, bully the investigators and pull strings, thinking they can handle this situation like they do everything else… with money, power and influence. Suffice it say, that when all is said and done, none of those things will help when dealing with depraved individuals. <br /><br />In the end, this is a pretty dark and twisted tale, and a compelling crime drama. <br /><br />4 stars<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9794972679291204094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <b>She wondered what it would have been like to have a son. Granted, she was an outsider, but mothers and sons seemed to have such uncomplicated relationships. Boys were easy to read. With one glance, you could tell whether they were angry or sad or happy. They appreciated simple things, like pizza and video games, and when they fought with their friends, it was never for blood, or worse, for sport. You never heard about boys writing slam notes or spreading rumors about each other at school. A boy never came home crying because someone called him fat. Well, maybe he did, but his mother could make everything better by stroking his head, baking some cookies. He would not sulk for weeks over the slightest perceived insult.” </b>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3163778010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3895801354706056956">3.5 Stars<br/><br/>Will Trent is intriguing, highly intelligent, soft spoken and a tad vulnerable. He’s fair haired, trim and wears suits to work as a member of Atlanta’s Georgia Bureau of Investigations. In case it’s not obvious, he basically sticks out like a sore thumb. <br/><br/>Now he is called in to investigate a crime that happens in an upscale community where a teenage girl was murdered and her assailant was murdered by the teenager’s mother when she happened upon the crime. It seems cut and dry yet Will Tr</span>
  <span id="freeText3895801354706056956" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br /><br />Will Trent is intriguing, highly intelligent, soft spoken and a tad vulnerable. He’s fair haired, trim and wears suits to work as a member of Atlanta’s Georgia Bureau of Investigations. In case it’s not obvious, he basically sticks out like a sore thumb. <br /><br />Now he is called in to investigate a crime that happens in an upscale community where a teenage girl was murdered and her assailant was murdered by the teenager’s mother when she happened upon the crime. It seems cut and dry yet Will Trent sees the crime through different eyes than everyone else, including the police on the scene.<br /><br />“Fractured” is the second novel in the “Will Trent” series with “Tryptich” being the first (which I have yet to read). It is my second foray into the Will Trent series and is giving me a flavor of the man Will Trent is. I am intrigued to know more about him, including where he came from, given how his mind works and how he solved the crimes in this novel. <br /><br />Thank you to my local library for a copy of this novel to borrow.<br /><br />Published on Goodreads on 2.17.20.<br /></span>

          </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415769066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2398583730117192823"><i>Originally posted on</i> <a href='http://wp.me/p3GvSV-5fK' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Nympho</a><br/><br/><b>Quick summary</b><br/>Abigail Campano comes home and interrupts what appears to be an intruder who's apparently murdered her daughter. What transpires next is shocking and extraordinary. The Georgia Bureau of Investigations (GBI) and Agent Will Trent are ultimately called in when the case extends beyond the reach of the Atlanta Police Department (APD). He's paired with APD Detective Faith Mitchell to coordinate the efforts of the two law enforcement groups and for the </span>
  <span id="freeText2398583730117192823" style="display:none"><i>Originally posted on</i> <a href="http://wp.me/p3GvSV-5fK" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Nympho</a><br /><br /><b>Quick summary</b><br />Abigail Campano comes home and interrupts what appears to be an intruder who's apparently murdered her daughter. What transpires next is shocking and extraordinary. The Georgia Bureau of Investigations (GBI) and Agent Will Trent are ultimately called in when the case extends beyond the reach of the Atlanta Police Department (APD). He's paired with APD Detective Faith Mitchell to coordinate the efforts of the two law enforcement groups and for the additional help. <br /><br /><b>What I loved about the story</b><br />Faith makes her debut in the story and I loved how her working relationship with Will evolved from nowhere to respect and grudging admiration. They made a great team, especially given Will's secret dyslexia. I'm looking forward to seeing more of them as a team. <br /><br />The case was extremely intriguing, taking some interesting and shocking twists and turns, some bordering on the macabre. The investigation was solid, showing the best of Will and his vulnerabilities. His relationship with fiancée Angie is a hot mess and it will be interesting to see where that goes. <br /><br /><b>The narration</b><br />Phil Gigante, one of my favorite narrators, provides a really good performance with perfect timing and character distinctions. <br /><br /><b>The bottom line</b><br />I really loved the odd connections between many of the characters. Atlanta is a big city where everyone seems to know everybody's history on some level. It's a southern thing that's well represented in the story. Slaughter is a master at weaving mystery, suspense and police procedurals with outstanding character development and this is a fine representation. I can't wait to start the next book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2398583730117192823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Especially since he has to work with a detective from the Atlanta PD who still hate him for catching some of their cops taking bribes to cover up drug dealing. Will has his own problems with his dyslexia and neglected childhood that make him socially awkward, but this all makes for a </span>
  <span id="freeText262833338535020089" style="display:none">After Detective Will Trent from the Georgia Bureau of Investigation walks into a crime scene in a wealthy Atlanta home with two teenagers dead and one missing, it was always going to be a complicated case to solve. Especially since he has to work with a detective from the Atlanta PD who still hate him for catching some of their cops taking bribes to cover up drug dealing. Will has his own problems with his dyslexia and neglected childhood that make him socially awkward, but this all makes for a fascinating character and one who sees things that others miss. Another great thriller from Karin Slaughter. Looking forward to reading more of this series. 4.5★</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1671686091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12348906745734453571">This is the second in the Will Trent series. In this one, Will Trent is called in to investigate the murder of a teenager girl. Upon finding her daughter dead, her Mother attacks who she believes to be her daughter's killer. It is also discovered that the missing girls father, knew Trent growing up.<br/><br/>Not everything is as it seems and we learn that one girl is dead while another is missing. Will and his new partner, Faith are working against the clock to find the missing teen.<br/><br/>I liked the character </span>
  <span id="freeText12348906745734453571" style="display:none">This is the second in the Will Trent series. In this one, Will Trent is called in to investigate the murder of a teenager girl. Upon finding her daughter dead, her Mother attacks who she believes to be her daughter's killer. It is also discovered that the missing girls father, knew Trent growing up.<br /><br />Not everything is as it seems and we learn that one girl is dead while another is missing. Will and his new partner, Faith are working against the clock to find the missing teen.<br /><br />I liked the character of Faith, who has a sort of past with Trent. Their interactions as first are hostile and apologetic. As the investigation goes on, we see Faith begin to warm up to Trent. <br /><br />Trent is still with on again off again girlfriend Angie. I hope he begins to wise up. He is so smart in many areas of his life and yet he keeps repeating the same mistake over and over again. He also seems to be stuck with his dyslexia, hiding it form his peers, ashamed and afraid of what they will think of him. He continues to awkward but the more we (I) learn about him, the more likable he becomes.<br /><br />The story is good and solid in this book. Like an onion this book has many layers and once peeled back, the story comes full swing.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>

  <span id="freeText9137245627760846527" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447508619i/17014240._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just getting started in this series and already I find myself getting sucked in fast! <b>Will Trent</b> is such and intriguing man He is a broken man. An awkward, eccentric personality. Yet he's also decent and kind. He is dysfunctional. He is brilliant. He is sexy as fuck, but in a shy and guarded sort of way. But more than anything... he is lonely. And yet he avoids close connections, they bring on too many questions. He has dreams, just like everyone else. But he buries them so deep that he's forgotten they even exist. And they terrify him. But I want this man to have everything. I want all of his dreams to come true. I wish I could make them come true. And still I know very little about him.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Will Trent was certainly an enigma.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>This is a crime series. It is violent and often gruesome. There is mystery and intrigue dripping off the pages. One of the things I like most about the series so far is the characters. They are so thick and juicy you can really sink your teeth into them. And many of them are not likable people. They are actually quite the opposite. (Except of course our lovely WT!)<br><br>This crime was actually quite complicated. I kept formulating new theories that all seemed to be wrong. I won't say much more about it, but it had my head spinning by the end. As soon as it all came into focus, I felt like going back to the beginning and reading it all over again to try to catch the clues. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Sometimes, all you could do was pray for the strength to carry on.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447508619i/17014241._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>For years, Abigail had worried that her daughter would turn out exactly like her mother. Now she worried the she would not turn out at all.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Anyway, I'm looking forward to moving on to the next book. I'm not joking about Will Trent. I am falling in love with him fast. And I don't even know why. But I'm afraid I'm a lost cause. <br><br>Angie is starting to piss me off. I want her gone. Will deserves better... no best.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447508619i/17014242._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Stay cool, Betty</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9137245627760846527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_398751797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/398751797" />
    <a title="Rick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8824769-rick"><img alt="Rick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360459107p2/8824769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/398751797?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick" href="/user/show/8824769-rick">Rick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer398751797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16425297047477466357">Yes, I've given "Fractured" 5 stars. NOT because it's the best book I've ever read, or because it's 'deep and meaningful literature.'<br/>I gave it five stars because it grabbed me, and kept me inside reading all weekend. And isn't THAT what a good mystery should do? There wasn't ever a good place to stop!<br/><br/>But there's many more positive things about "Fractured" that should be said:<br/>The main character is Will Trent, a member of the Georgia Bureau of Investigation. He's complex, has a deep and troubled b</span>
  <span id="freeText16425297047477466357" style="display:none">Yes, I've given "Fractured" 5 stars. NOT because it's the best book I've ever read, or because it's 'deep and meaningful literature.'<br />I gave it five stars because it grabbed me, and kept me inside reading all weekend. And isn't THAT what a good mystery should do? There wasn't ever a good place to stop!<br /><br />But there's many more positive things about "Fractured" that should be said:<br />The main character is Will Trent, a member of the Georgia Bureau of Investigation. He's complex, has a deep and troubled background but never becomes trite or predictable. Will is teamed with Faith Mitchell, an Atlanta cop, with baggage of her own. And here's where I was surprised...there were so many common roads Slaughter could have mistakenly taken with this combination and DIDN'T. Their partnership could have been 'too cute'(wasn't!), or Trent could get all 'MALE' with Faith(DIDN'T!).<br /><br />I admit(perhaps by even saying this, I'm exposing MY sexist views?)to being worried that a female author MIGHT write her female characters somewhat...defensively. Slaughter's women characters are well-rounded, varied and realistic. There's no apologies for women in leadership roles who could be considered..er..overbearing, nor is there the perennial female victim. There are no stereotypes here. Ultimately, what Slaughter has given her readers are PEOPLE that drive this excellent story.<br /><br />And it was the STORY kept me on the edge of my Kindle. You've probably read a synopsis somewhere, so I won't go over the storyline with you. But let me share the fact that there's a whole lot more going on than meets the eye!<br /><br />Buy it, reserve some time for yourself and enjoy</span>
  <a data-text-id="16425297047477466357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2842561117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17928121825000252800">This was the second in the Will Trent mystery series by Karin Slaughter. I am hard pressed to find anything to complain about because, as I've said before, she's just such a fine writer. <br/><br/>The story this time focused much more around family than the others I have read, and in a few places I seriously cried. It had a major creative twist at the beginning that I never could have seen coming. Taughtly written with precision and grace, Fractured was a slam dunk.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_52679236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52679236" />
    <a title="Jaime" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/159833-jaime"><img alt="Jaime" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536077538p2/159833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52679236?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime" href="/user/show/159833-jaime">Jaime</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/159833-jaime?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/159833-jaime?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/159833-jaime?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52679236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1425622851421792836">I really loved Triptych when I read it, but it took me some time to warm up to Fractured. Will Trent is a very unconventional main character — after all, he’s a GBI investigator that can’t read. He’s awkward, socially inept, and at times, easily flustered. I tend to waffle back and forth in my belief of the scenario but by the time I get to the end, I have to admit that I feel for him. Slaughter takes his illiteracy and really makes it matter, as his dyslexia leads to him discovering some key fa</span>
  <span id="freeText1425622851421792836" style="display:none">I really loved Triptych when I read it, but it took me some time to warm up to Fractured. Will Trent is a very unconventional main character — after all, he’s a GBI investigator that can’t read. He’s awkward, socially inept, and at times, easily flustered. I tend to waffle back and forth in my belief of the scenario but by the time I get to the end, I have to admit that I feel for him. Slaughter takes his illiteracy and really makes it matter, as his dyslexia leads to him discovering some key facts later than he should. I’m glad she’s decided to give him a partner and really test his comfort zone. I think it makes him more of a fully flushed-out character, and that’s why I root for him in the end.<br /><br />But enough about Will! The real mystery here, What Has Happened to Emma?, is a good one. Not only is this the story of a brutal kidnapping (or murder? or both?), but much like in Triptych, you’re never completely sure who are the good guys and who are the bad. Also, Slaughter does a good job of telling a story about the foster care system, and how shared upbringings can have very different results. There is not yet a third book in this series, but I hope there will be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1425622851421792836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3049969849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3049969849" />
    <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe"><img alt="Amanda Hupe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535036536p2/11658047.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3049969849?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Hupe" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe">Amanda Hupe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11658047-amanda-hupe?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3049969849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16950862284059674130">So I read Fractured by Karin Slaughter in a day. You know those times when you get some popcorn and watch a scary movie alone at night and you are just stuffing the popcorn in your face, not blinking at the TV screen. Yeah, that is how I am when I read any Karin Slaughter book. This time, instead of popcorn it is a red velvet bundt cake.<br/><br/>This is the second book in the Will Trent Series. In true Karin Slaughter fashion, it starts off with the brutal murder of a teen girl. Will Trent and his boss A</span>
  <span id="freeText16950862284059674130" style="display:none">So I read Fractured by Karin Slaughter in a day. You know those times when you get some popcorn and watch a scary movie alone at night and you are just stuffing the popcorn in your face, not blinking at the TV screen. Yeah, that is how I am when I read any Karin Slaughter book. This time, instead of popcorn it is a red velvet bundt cake.<br /><br />This is the second book in the Will Trent Series. In true Karin Slaughter fashion, it starts off with the brutal murder of a teen girl. Will Trent and his boss Amanda are brought in to assist the police department. However, after a thorough examination of the crime scene. One girl is dead, but another girl named Emma may have been kidnapped. Will Trent usually works alone, but he is assigned a partner in this case. Faith Mitchell’s mother was involved in an investigation ran by Will Trent. So emotions are tense between the two, but there is no doubt they make a good team. Can they find the murderer and save Emma in time?<br /><br />One thing I always appreciate with Karin Slaughter books is that I am never disappointed. I never find her books predictable either. This book especially! I found myself shocked more than once. This book has excellent twists, turns, and diversions. The suspense kept me up until 1 am until I finished the book. There is not one moment where I thought the book is dull or slow. I was fully engaged from the beginning. So much so, it took every bit of control I possess to not get up, go to the library, and get book 3 called Undone. But my TBR is calling my name.<br /><br />Anyway, as always, I love Will Trent. I think Faith Mitchell is going to be a great partner for him. He is dyslexic and struggles with being open about it. However, his observation in crime scenes is off the charts. He is such a brilliant character.<br /><br />One thing about these books, if you are not into violence, this may not be the book for you. Karin Slaughter is very descriptive about the crime scenes. I actually appreciate that aspect, because it makes me feel like I am there and a part of the investigation. Anyway, 5 out of 5 stars from me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16950862284059674130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2559930651767301008">This is the second in the Will Trent series and in this installment Will is directed to work with Faith, his future partner, for the first time. They are assigned to a murder, kidnapping case where Will has a tumultuous personal history with one of the victims Fathers, which he chooses to keep to himself. Will and Faith are forced to come together and start building some bonds quickly in order to save one of the </span>
  <span id="freeText2559930651767301008" style="display:none">This is the second in the Will Trent series and in this installment Will is directed to work with Faith, his future partner, for the first time. They are assigned to a murder, kidnapping case where Will has a tumultuous personal history with one of the victims Fathers, which he chooses to keep to himself. A good thriller that has everyone stumped in the beginning with virtually no leads. Will and Faith are forced to come together and start building some bonds quickly in order to save one of the victims who was kidnapped. Karin Slaughter has a way of keeping each of her books original, she is consistsnt with her fast moving, smart, and always intence, crime thriller story lines. This series is up towards the top of my list and I recommend it to anyone who enjoys this genre. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971162382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9126030221891159183">Because I haven't read the first book,probably that's why it was a bit hard for me to understand the relationship between the characters and their background. But still... <br/><br/>The story revolves around a murder and an abduction. 2 best friends,looking so similar that even the mother becomes confused -_- . Everyone thinks the victim is Emma Campano,the daughter of an unbelievably rich couple. Only the father is able to recognize that it is indeed NOT his daughter,but her best friend. So weird. How ca</span>
  <span id="freeText9126030221891159183" style="display:none">Because I haven't read the first book,probably that's why it was a bit hard for me to understand the relationship between the characters and their background. But still... <br /><br />The story revolves around a murder and an abduction. 2 best friends,looking so similar that even the mother becomes confused -_- . Everyone thinks the victim is Emma Campano,the daughter of an unbelievably rich couple. Only the father is able to recognize that it is indeed NOT his daughter,but her best friend. So weird. How can a mother not recognize her own daughter??? Also,when her daughter's boyfriend comes down for help,she kills him with her bare hand taking him as the murderer. Turns out,Emma is abducted and there comes Will Trent to find her.<br /><br />There are so many things about the book that I didn't like. Will-Angie-Faith-Angela - I still can't decipher their behavior throughout the novel. Also,some unimportant characters were highlighted a lot but on the other hand,the parents of the murdered teens seemed as passive as possible,which is very unlikely. Then there are the villains. there are 2 villains apparently,which makes it harder to find Emma. From killing with brutality to rape and sodomy,the novel has everything. Want a very very ruthless villain? Try this book.<br /><br />Did I like the novel?- maybe. Will I read the next book?- maybe no. But then again,it's just my own perspective.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9126030221891159183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13205522213540701090">Karin Slaughter books are always a sure thing.<br/><br/>For me the goal of this book was less about solving the crime and more about getting to know Will better. Will has a new partner who has every reason to exploit his weaknesses. In an effort to hide his dyslexia he inevitably makes mistakes that may jeopardise the whole investigation.<br/><br/>And the clock is ticking….<br/><br/>An affluent young teenager has been abducted, leaving in her wake a dead best friend and unknown young man. The crime scene gets compromised fro</span>
  <span id="freeText13205522213540701090" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter books are always a sure thing.<br /><br />For me the goal of this book was less about solving the crime and more about getting to know Will better. Will has a new partner who has every reason to exploit his weaknesses. In an effort to hide his dyslexia he inevitably makes mistakes that may jeopardise the whole investigation.<br /><br />And the clock is ticking….<br /><br />An affluent young teenager has been abducted, leaving in her wake a dead best friend and unknown young man. The crime scene gets compromised from the get go, there are no leads and skeletons from Will’s past comes back to haunt him.<br /><br />A steady plot, a slightly slower pace than expected but still well worth the read.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O23FN3K+gWJXYWKA01IE4vxaU9eiNVmrVoh1Xopi3acnL9KdDCHJTb5phQnybZSOHelmFOGXfjv88vgZQMexxg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F1oDOuK3ixW7nTKvbOBHvFa50Ke2FWjMZzIpu+x7J/oLGBSQnCjDOlKV1SZN39fQtwrlZPW3T1zNSKT8Jt5Lmw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10037314787844604441">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER.   <span id="freeText10037314787844604441" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAST WIDOW, features Sara Linton and Will Trent. Slaughter is the founder of the Save the Libraries project—a nonprofit organization established to support libraries and library programming. A native of Georgia, Karin Slaughter lives in Atlanta. Her standalone novels PIECES OF HER, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and COP TOWN are in development for film and television.<br /><br /><br /><b>Facebook:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter">Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter</a> <br /><br /><b>Website</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.karinslaughter.com/">http://www.karinslaughter.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Instagram</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/karinslaughterauthor/">https://www.instagram.com/karinslaugh...</a><br /></span>
